D36-a (owner ruling 2026-07-20, corpus-relative): COMMON_GRAM_DF/RARE_LEMMA_DF in query/parallels.rb stop being frozen absolutes and become max(floor, round(RATIO × live passage count)), snapshot once per run (#snapshot_cutoffs reads the corpus's passage high-water mark as `@catalog[:passages].max(:id)` — an O(1) B-tree max, instant, vs the ~40 s count(*) on 24.4M rows; nil trips the absolute fallback). The ratios are the tuning numerators verbatim — Rational(500, 3_760_000) ≈ 133 ppm and Rational(2_000, 3_760_000) ≈ 532 ppm — so at the 3.76M tuning size the cutoffs reproduce 500/2,000 exactly, and the tuning constants survive as the FLOOR (binding below tuning size, so tiny test corpora are never over-pruned — the cognates max(STOP_MIN_DF, …) pattern) AND the unavailable-count fallback. BEFORE/AFTER (measured live read-only): the absolute-500 cutoff had decayed to 20.5 ppm of the settled corpus (from 133 ppm at tuning — 6.5× too tight, silently narrowing recall as the corpus quadrupled); the relative cutoff restores 133 ppm = 3,247 (common) / 12,987 (rare) at 24.4M. The pinned Matthew 4:4 / LXX Deut 8:3 case: its 12 folded 4-grams probe live at df 4–18 (all far under BOTH cutoffs — a real quotation's grams are rare, so this pair was never at risk either way; the corpus-relative fix matters for the band of grams sitting between 500 and 3,247, which absolute-500 was wrongly dropping). TDD: 4 new parallels_test cases pin the ratio math, the snapshot at 24.4M (→3,247/12,987), the floor below tuning, and the nil-count fallback (singleton override, no minitest/mock). 2026-07-20 · P36-2 · TBD · Bulk-load engineering — rebuild-only pragmas + per-source batch transactions + deferred secondary indexes, each measured on a synthetic fixture-corpus baseline via the P36-0 profiler (the instrument), rebuild output pinned BYTE-IDENTICAL (doc/passage/fts content-shas + row/lemma counts unchanged across every variant). MEASUREMENT HARNESS (scratchpad, not committed — gitignored worktree material): 5-source / 7,800-doc / 49,000-passage deterministic corpus (annotated variant → 416,498 lemma rows to exercise the fts_lemma path), min-over-4-warm-runs to beat ~9% run-to-run wall noise. (1) REBUILD-MODE PRAGMAS (Store.rebuild_pragmas! + `rebuild:` kwarg on Store.connect/connect_fulltext; rebuild.rb fresh_db + connect_fulltext pass it): synchronous=OFF + cache_size=-262144 (256 MiB) + temp_store=MEMORY, layered ON TOP of WAL (WAL STAYS — keeps the P17-7 concurrent-reader-no-BusyException guarantee; synchronous=OFF is the durability knob under it). CRASH SEMANTICS, stated in code + here: the corruption window is power-loss / OS-crash (NOT a clean process abort), and it is FINE — the derived db is a pure function of canonical/, so a crashed rebuild is simply RE-RUN (rm + rebuild), never recovered; NEVER on the live sync path (a sync crash must not corrupt the live-read catalog). Alone this is within noise (~1%: WAL already softens fsync and 49k per-doc commits dominate) — kept because it is the correct foundation and compounds with (2)/(4) + the big cache/temp_store aid the index builds. (2) PER-SOURCE BATCH TRANSACTIONS (Loader#tx_batch, nil=sync path unchanged, Integer=rebuild): the plain Loader batched N parsed docs into ONE transaction, each under a per-document SAVEPOINT so a constraint-violating doc still rolls back only itself while its batch siblings commit — the per-document isolation the sync path gets from a top-level transaction, preserved (new tests pin it). Rebuild passes LOAD_TX_BATCH=1000; measured 200/1000/5000/single-source-tx (batch=∞) all flat (insert 6.33–6.36 s) → FIXED batch matches the mega-transaction's speed WITHOUT its uncommitted-WAL-frame ceiling (the cdli 353k-doc concern), so fixed 1000 chosen. DictionaryLoader studied and LEFT ALONE: already per-FILE (coarse — a file holds many entries; the reflex-bearing hotspots are single-file kaikki, so per-file == per-source) — it has no per-document-transaction problem, so batching it would be an un-measured change. Insert 7.71→7.04 s (annotated corpus, cumulative with 1). (3) DEFERRED SECONDARY INDEXES (Store.DEFERRED_REBUILD_INDEXES + drop_deferred_indexes!/create_deferred_indexes!; rebuild.rb drops after migrate!, recreates after the replay before the query-side stages): the migration-aware clean seam — an applied migration is NEVER edited; rebuild drops/recreates the INDEX objects only. ENUMERATION (STRICTLY non-unique query accelerators — dropping them can never change output): passages.document_id (001) + passages.language (013) + provenance.passage_id (001) + provenance.document_id (001) — the two highest-insert-volume replay tables. DELIBERATELY EXCLUDED: every unique/identity index (documents.urn, passages.urn, passages.(document_id,sequence) — they enforce identity AND back the loader's insert-time lookups: dropping passages.urn would turn each fresh-insert Document.first(urn) into a full scan, a catastrophe, not a win) and documents.source_id (the per-source withdrawal sweep needs it live). Insert 7.04→6.18 s (plain corpus) / present on annotated too. (4) FTS-SIDE (Indexer): create_lemma_table now creates the passage_lemmas table BARE; new create_lemma_indexes builds its three B-tree indexes (lemma_folded/urn/language) in one sorted pass AFTER the bulk insert, still inside the fts_lemma stage and BEFORE the reflex pass that reads them — the same defer-then-bulk-build trick on the derived-of-derived db, which also now rides the rebuild-mode pragma connection. fts_lemma 4.07→3.88 s over 416k lemma rows. FTS5 external/contentless-content (avoid storing text_normalized twice) DEFERRED and journaled as a candidate: the win is real (text copy is a big share of the 16m live index) but the diff is wide (refresh_source!'s delete-by-rowid contract + query paths assume a REGULAR contentful table) — small-diffs rule, a future packet. NET on the annotated fixture corpus: grand 14.51→13.62 s (−6.1%), insert 7.71→7.04 (−8.7%), fts_lemma 4.07→3.88 (−4.7%) — all byte-identical. PROJECTION (honest — fixture is the instrument, NOT the live scale): the live rebuild (owner's settled numbers) is per-source load ~2h05m (insert-bound, cdli 353k docs @0.0014 s/doc the exemplar) + FTS index 16m16s + timeline 58.4s + facets 59.0s over 24.4M passages. The insert-side wins (batch transactions + provenance/passages index deferral) scale with row volume — provenance alone is ~24M+ journal inserts × 2 deferred indexes live vs 56.8k × 2 on the fixture — so the ~9–12% fixture insert reduction is a conservative floor for the load phase (bigger tables = more per-row index maintenance avoided); the lemma-index deferral scales with the 2.8M live lemma rows (vs 416k fixture). NOT projected: the FTS text-tokenize bulk (the dominant 16m share) is untouched by these changes — that is the external-content refactor's target, journaled. NOT TOUCHED (P36-1 parallel region): rebuild's derivation-stamp / --incremental hunks; my edits stay in connection setup, transaction grain, index deferral — overlaps for the orchestrator. 2026-07-20 · P36-1 · 09e92e2 · Derivation stamps + `rebuild --incremental` (fable, worktree). THE FINGERPRINT (Nabu::DerivationFingerprint, four-input rule + registry posture): (1) canonical bytes — embedded git repos contribute HEAD sha (O(1) for the big clones; nested repos each counted, the kanripo shape) PLUS the git-excluded `.attic/` content hashed explicitly (canonical data git can't vouch for); non-git trees (zip/file/wiki/sefaria fetches, local shelves) get a full sha256 tree-content digest — stronger than the fetchers' own `.zip-fetch.json`/`.file-fetch.json` archive shas, mtime-blind, O(bytes) but cheap vs parse; a git tree with non-attic porcelain output (hand edits, untracked files, LFS materialization — cdli will read so) is WEAK identity: nil fingerprint, no stamp, NEVER skipped (over-rebuild safe, under-rebuild the sin). (2) parser code — per-FAMILY granularity via a constant-reference BFS closure over lib/nabu/adapters/ (declaration map from class/module lines minus the Nabu/Adapters namespace wrappers; one union-regex pass per file): catches Perseus→EpidocParser composition that require_relative scanning MISSES (perseus.rb never requires its parser — the require-graph design was rejected on exactly this), follows subclassing (First1kGreek→Perseus→epidoc), over-approximates safely; plus a shared derivation-core digest of everything else under lib/nabu/ minus an EXCLUSION list (mcp/query/health/ops, CLI/display, fetch layer, batch producers — asymmetric by design: a forgotten exclusion over-rebuilds, an include-list omission would under-rebuild) + the alignments.yml content. (3) fold rules — digest of normalize.rb (auto-honest; a hand-bumped version constant can be forgotten). (4) migration level. (5) entry flags translations/classes/lemma_tier/fuzzy_index as plain config_json (they change derived rows with zero byte/code change — the gap the four-input rule alone would miss). STORAGE: `derivation_stamps` IN the catalog (migration 017; slug PK, fingerprint + the five components + stamped_at; Store::DerivationStamp module seam), dropped+re-stamped by every full rebuild (Rebuild#replay stamps — correct by construction), absent row = dirty. INCREMENTAL (Nabu::IncrementalRebuild < Rebuild, new file — rebuild.rb hunks kept surgical for the P36-0 merge): reuses the inherited replay seam verbatim (sync_source! + content-kind loader full:true upsert/withdraw/revise + RunRecorder kind=rebuild + quarantine baseline) + Indexer.refresh_source! per dirty non-inert source (row-identity contract already pinned, P26-5; reflexes_changed on dictionary grains; missing/pre-tier fulltext self-heals via the internal full-reindex fallback); timeline+facets re-run corpus-wide only when ≥1 source was dirty (no per-source seam — the honest list; links journal untouched, exactly like full rebuild). LOUD REFUSALS (never silent divergence): no catalog / schema_info ≠ code's migration level ("full rebuild required") / orphan rows+stamps for unreplayable slugs (a full rebuild would drop them). `--dry-run --incremental` = per-source clean/dirty verdict naming the drifted component, byte-touch-free (test-pinned). THE SACRED TEST (test/rebuild_incremental_test.rb, 3-source corpus: 2×TestAdapter + lexica dictionary): full → dirty ONE byte in beta → incremental re-derives beta ONLY, alpha/lexica untouched at ROW IDENTITY (whole-row compare, ids+revisions), final state ≡ a fresh full rebuild of the same tree into a second db_dir (urn-keyed content shas for documents/passages/dictionary_entries + fts rows + axes/facets counts); plus stamp-missing=dirty, fold-digest change dirties ALL, schema-behind and no-catalog and orphan refusals, nothing-dirty = byte-level no-op with builders skipped. Honest divergences documented (architecture §1/§5): ids, revisions (incremental journals MORE history), sources.last_sync_* mirrors, withdrawn tombstones; syncs don't stamp (stale stamp = one safe re-derive); gems/Ruby not fingerprinted. Files: lib/nabu/{derivation_fingerprint,incremental_rebuild}.rb + store/derivation_stamp.rb + migration 017 new; rebuild.rb (stamp hunk), cli.rb (--incremental + printers), store.rb, nabu.rb wiring. Tests +28 (fingerprint 15, incremental 10, cli 3). Suite 4,889 runs / 72,966 assertions exit 0 · rubocop 595 files exit 0 (worktree). OWNER QUEUE: after the live reindex settles, `nabu rebuild` once (writes the first stamps), then `nabu rebuild --incremental --dry-run` to see the corpus verdict.

2026-07-20 · P36-0 · fd07301 · The rebuild profiler — always-on per-source/per-stage wall-time capture behind `rebuild --profile` (§6b: numbers before optimization; tiers P36-2/P36-3). New `Nabu::RebuildProfile` (lib/nabu/rebuild_profile.rb): an in-memory `[scope,stage]→seconds` collector, one `Process.clock_gettime(CLOCK_MONOTONIC)` pair per stage boundary (per DOCUMENT for parse/insert — never per passage, the always-on budget), NEVER persisted, so rebuild-safe by construction (nothing under db/ to regenerate). Two levels: a per-source `:load` roll-up (measured around the whole replay in Rebuild#run — authoritative, includes adapter build/run-recorder) with `:parse`/`:insert` COMPONENTS folded inside it (so parse+insert ≲ load and are never re-summed into the grand total), plus corpus stages `:timeline`/`:facets` (around the two builders) and — threaded into `Indexer.rebuild!` via a new `profile:` kwarg + `timed` helper — `:fts_lemma`/`:trigram`/`:alignment`/`:reflex`. fts_lemma is ONE stage on purpose: the FTS tokenize and lemma-index build share Indexer#insert_passage_batches' single streaming row scan, inseparable without a per-passage timer (said honestly in code + report). Loader seam: `profile:` kwarg on Store::Loader + Store::DictionaryLoader (the corpus-mass loaders) wraps `adapter.parse` and the per-doc insert transaction; nil on the sync path (SyncRunner unaffected — zero overhead) and on the 3 tiny dossier/note shelf loaders (they show only their :load roll-up, no split). CLI: `rebuild --profile` prints the heaviest-first table (per-source loads + corpus stages, each with its share of the grand total) then a stage-share summary (parse/insert within load; corpus index total; GRAND TOTAL) — opt-in, print-only; `--dry-run` implies nothing extra; the existing kept-on stage lines on stderr are untouched (the pinned ["corpus","timeline","facets","fulltext index"] stage list is unchanged — no behaviour change to what rebuild builds). Result gains a `profile:` field (defaults nil). LIVE recovery (honest, read-only ?mode=ro against db/history.sqlite3 — the owner's rebuild was mid corpus-wide reindex): the ledger's kind=rebuild run rows gave COARSE per-source LOAD wall-times (parse+insert combined — no split; the split lands NEXT rebuild on this instrumented code) for the current run — 80 sources, ~7,206 s (~2h0m) total load, heaviest cbeta 1308 s / kanripo 1067 s / gretil 605 s / cdli 503 s / oracc 391 s / diorisis 316 s / imp 278 s / dcs 250 s / coptic-scriptorium 208 s / lexica 198 s / papyri 175 s / edh 160 s; the TEI mega-sources are few-doc/high-parse-cost (cbeta 0.36 s/doc) vs tabular sources many-doc/insert-cost (cdli 0.0014 s/doc). The corpus-wide reindex produces NO ledger row and was STILL running (fulltext WAL 3.3→4.1 GB, 15:51→15:57+) — its duration is NOT recoverable read-only and lands next rebuild. Fixture-scale calibration (9 real fixtures, isolated tmpdir): grand 0.70 s, load 0.65 s (parse 0.31 ≈ insert 0.28), corpus index only 0.05 s (7%) — which CAN indicate per-passage parse-vs-insert ratios (coptic parse-heavy ~69%; tabular insert-heavy) but CANNOT predict the live corpus-wide index share (O(4.3M passages), trivial at 1006). Dispatch: P36-2 (bulk-load) GO — insert + the minutes-long reindex are both large targets; P36-3 (parallel parse) WARRANTED but confirm on the parse/insert split from the next instrumented rebuild — the recovered load times concentrate ~2,000 s+ of wall time in a handful of parse-bound TEI sources, but the ledger can't prove parse-vs-insert alone. Tests: test/rebuild_profile_test.rb (10, arithmetic/monotonic/sums with a fake clock), rebuild_test.rb (+1: Result carries a profile, stages present, parse+insert≤load, grand=load+index), cli_test.rb (+3: --profile table shape, absent without flag, no-op on dry-run). Files: lib/nabu/rebuild_profile.rb (new), lib/nabu.rb, lib/nabu/rebuild.rb, lib/nabu/store/{loader,dictionary_loader,indexer}.rb, lib/nabu/cli.rb, docs/backlog.md (P36-0 → done), this line. No schema, no canonical/db write, no network. Not pushed, not merged.

2026-07-04 · P3-4 · 5715a01 · ProielParser (third parser family, streaming sibling to Epidoc/Conllu) + PROIEL adapter. Parser: Nokogiri::XML::Reader single pass (sources reach ~29 MB, never DOMed — code-structure test enforces it), reacts only to <source>/<sentence>/<token> so the whole <annotation> dictionary block streams past unslurped (token attrs already carry the terse codes; the dicts only label them). sentence = passage, urn = <doc-urn>:<sentence/@id> verbatim (stable upstream db keys, non-contiguous — 88119/88118 interleaved among 86xxx — never renumbered); sequence = kept order from 0. text = per token presentation-before + form + presentation-after (PROIEL's surface encoding — spacing/punct live in the attrs, not element boundaries), NFC; text_normalized = NFC(downcase). Empty tokens (empty-token-sort, no form) contribute nothing to text but stay in annotations. annotations = {"tokens"=>[{id,form,lemma,part_of_speech,morphology,head_id,relation,citation_part,information_status,empty_token_sort} nils dropped], "citation"=>first token's citation-part, "status"=>sentence/@status}; <slash> secondary edges ignored. Cross-checks → ParseError: <source id> ≠ urn tail, <source language> ≠ caller language (caller wins but disagreement surfaced), missing sentence/@id (names file + document-order position), zero sentences. Adapter: manifest id proiel / name "PROIEL Treebank" / license_class nc / upstream proiel-treebank / parser_family proiel; discover walks <workdir>/*.xml, peeks each <source> header via Reader (id/language/<title>, stops at first <div>), one DocumentRef per file urn:nabu:proiel:<source-id> (== parse urn, conformance identity), skips files w/o <source> defensively; parse delegates; fetch = single-repo Perseus git clone/pull + FetchReport. Registered proiel (enabled:false, sync_policy:frozen — repo frozen at 20180408, successor syntacticus-treebank-data noted). Tests: parser unit against real fixture (18 passages, first urn …:86000, text "Quamquam te, Marce fili…"→"orationis facultate.", presentation-before "(nihil", lemma quamquam/pos G-/citation 1.1, empty-token kept-but-textless, dropped-nil head-id, language/source-id/missing-id/zero-sentence/malformed errors, IO+streaming checks) + AdapterConformance + discover-1-ref + skip-non-treebank + local-git fetch + registry round-trip. 2026-07-04 · P4-1 · 8ffadb0 · FTS5 fulltext index + Nabu::Store::Indexer. Separate db/fulltext.sqlite3 (arch §2 one-file-per-concern; catalog stays small/precious, index disposable): Config#fulltext_path + Store.connect_fulltext (reuses connect's scheme-less-path handling, no FK pragma). Indexer.rebuild!(catalog:,fulltext:) drops+recreates ONE FTS5 virtual table passages_fts(text_normalized, urn UNINDEXED, passage_id UNINDEXED, tokenize unicode61 remove_diacritics 2) — created imperatively here, NOT a numbered migration (migrations own the catalog only; the index is derived-of-derived, rebuilt at will; the raw db.run heredoc DDL is the sole sanctioned SQL string — virtual-table DDL has no Sequel dataset API, query paths stay on datasets), bulk-inserts (each_slice 2000 multi_insert, one txn) every passage that is live AND under a live document (P1-4 two-level visibility, joined through documents via raw datasets independent of global model binding), returns count. Auto-wired: SyncRunner reindexes after each successful (non-aborted) sync AFTER the RunRecorder block (corpus-wide, not per-source — an indexing failure is its own error, never a falsified run row; parse-only reindexes too), Rebuild reindexes once after all sources replayed (drops the fulltext file too); both carry the count in their Outcome/Result and the CLI prints "indexed N passages". KEY FINDING/DECISION: SQLite 3.53.2's unicode61 remove_diacritics 2 does NOT fold precomposed polytonic Greek (verified: ά/ῆ/ἀ/ῃ all unfolded; it strips only a few *combining* marks and only in NFD — never perispomeni/breathings/iota-subscript), and the corpus stores text_normalized as NFC, so the tokenizer ALONE cannot deliver Greek diacritic-insensitive search. Resolution (in scope, honoring arch §3 "text_normalized = diacritic-folded search form"): the Indexer folds via new Nabu::Normalize.fold_diacritics (NFD → drop \p{Mn} → NFC) before indexing; the catalog's text_normalized is untouched (adapters still only lowercase — deeper per-language fold at the adapter boundary is a future packet needing a corpus reload). P4-2 MUST fold the query with the same function (MATCH via db[:passages_fts].where(Sequel.lit("passages_fts MATCH ?", Normalize.fold_diacritics(q))); snippet() available as Sequel.function(:snippet, Sequel.lit("passages_fts"), …) but returns the FOLDED form, so display should render the catalog's pristine text joined via passage_id). Tests: indexer unit (live count, withdrawn-passage + withdrawn-document exclusion, idempotent no-dupes, μῆνιν findable by μηνιν, passage_id linkback) + fold_diacritics unit (polytonic/Latin/no-op/NFC) + SyncRunner & Rebuild & CLI integration (index populated, parse-only reindexes, aborted has no count). Suite 407/3503 green, lint clean.
2026-07-04 · P4-2 · 321beec · `nabu search` + Nabu::Query::Search (new lib/nabu/query/ layer, arch §2). Search.new(catalog:,fulltext:).run(query, lang:, license:, limit:20) → array of Result(urn, language, text, snippet, document_title, license_class). Pipeline: fold+downcase the query with the SAME Normalize.fold_diacritics the Indexer used (the fold-both-sides contract — else accented↔unaccented misses) → FTS5 MATCH (Sequel.lit "passages_fts MATCH ?" parameter-bound, the sole user-text-in-SQL point) ordered by bm25(passages_fts) with a generous inner limit (limit*10) → collect passage_ids in rank order → TWO-STEP id join into the catalog (no ATTACH: index is a separate SQLite file) through passages⋈documents⋈sources applying NOT passage.withdrawn AND NOT document.withdrawn + optional language equality + optional license equality on coalesce(documents.license_override, sources.license_class) (P1-3 override wins) → reassemble in FTS rank order, trim to limit, attach snippet. DECISIONS: (1) license filter is EXACT-CLASS in v1 (--license open ≠ "at least as open"); permissiveness ordering deferred, documented in the class header. (2) snippet() is the FTS highlight over the FOLDED index column so its accents are STRIPPED — it marks WHERE the match is, not the source spelling; the pristine accented text rides in Result#text for display, and the CLI footer labels the highlight "(highlights are diacritic-folded)". (3) bm25/snippet ride as literal SQL fragments (FTS auxiliary functions, no Sequel dataset API — same sanctioned-exception class as the Indexer DDL); no user input in them. CLI: search QUERY [--lang X] [--license CLASS] [--limit N] — validates --license against SourceManifest::LICENSE_CLASSES up front (unknown → exit 1 listing the enum), empty query → exit 1; missing/never-built index (fulltext file absent OR passages_fts table absent, via open_fulltext helper) → "no index — run nabu sync or nabu rebuild" exit 1; zero hits → "no matches" exit 0; hits render "urn [lang]" + folded-snippet line + "N hit(s)" footer. Removed search from the not-implemented CLI stub loop. 2026-07-04 · P5-1 · b31fbb4 · Restart-aware DdbdpParser urn minting (the 12,288 duplicate-urn quarantine class from the 2026-07-04 first sync). Citation shape extended: urn = <doc-urn>[:<textpart-path>][:b<k>]:<lb n> — the implicit restart block b<k> (k ≥ 2), shaped like a synthetic textpart, sits between textpart path and line number. Blocks open on URN COLLISION, not numeric comparison: when a line's default suffix equals one already minted in this document (within the same textpart context — counter resets at every textpart boundary), the next block opens (b2, b3, …) and the line re-mints inside it, looping until unique; the first block never carries a label. Collision-triggered IS the frozen-urn safety argument: any document that parsed cleanly pre-P5-1 had zero suffix collisions by definition, so the mechanism provably never engages and its urns stay byte-identical (a monotonicity heuristic could fire on loaded docs with odd-but-unique @n like "12/13" and silently re-mint frozen urns); restart docs never entered the catalog, so their urns were free to define. Trade-off documented in the parser header: a restart beginning at a number the previous block never reached opens its block only at the first collision (urns unique+stable, merely blind to that boundary). VERIFIED EMPIRICALLY (read-only vs live catalog): 1,000 random loaded papyri docs re-parsed → 0 urn mismatches; ALL 12,287 duplicate-urn quarantined docs re-parsed → 12,287 recover clean with unique urns, 0 still failing. Exemplar aegyptus.89.240 (flat <ab>, lb n=1 twice, lb n=11 twice) mints :1, :b2:1…:b2:11, :b3:11 (13 passages). Fixtures: aegyptus.89.240.xml + text-less stub chrest.wilck.101.xml copied whole (small; no trimming needed) from local canonical snapshot into test/fixtures/papyri-ddbdp/ + README w/ provenance; pre-existing ddbdp fixtures/conformance workdir untouched. Tests: restart parse w/ full expected urn list + uniqueness, text spot-checks, stability across two parses, GOLDEN regression asserting all three pre-P5-1 fixture urn lists byte-identical, stub still quarantines w/ clear message naming the file. Also: .rubocop.yml now excludes canonical/** — rake lint was ALREADY broken on this box (first torot sync pulled upstream .rb tooling into gitignored canonical/), not this diff. STUB-CLASS AUDIT (9,351 "no citable lines"; all 9,351 machine-classified from the quarantine journal + ~20 hand-inspected): 9,220 literally empty <ab/> + ~40 whitespace-only <ab> + 2 self-closing edition divs — genuine cross-reference stubs (header <ref type="reprint-in"> names the republication), correctly quarantined; 33 note-only + a few figure-only (drawings) — genuinely text-less. (1) Liveness = `git ls-remote <url> HEAD` → :alive (+HEAD sha) / :gone (Shell::Error) / :moved (best-effort: git output looks like a 301/redirect — honest that git usually follows GitHub's rename silently so most renames read :alive against the new location); only :gone sets exit 1, :moved is a soft "stored URL stale" signal, detail carries git's first stderr line. Two-callers-one-module: lib/nabu/health/trend_rules.rb holds every threshold ONCE (Health::Finding{kind,severity,message}; severity drives both the CLI label and the exit code), consumed by lib/nabu/health/local_check.rb (whole-history health report) and SyncRunner#deviation_warnings (one fresh LoadReport). SOFT/LOUD SPLIT (loud = exit 1 red; soft = exit 0 advisory; info = never affects exit): (1) quarantine_spike LOUD — latest successful run's errored > max(prior ≤5 runs) AND > SPIKE_FLOOR=10, so 0→1/2→7 never scream and a first sync with no prior norm is never a spike; (2) added_collapse SOFT — last COLLAPSE_RUNS=3 successful runs all added:0 AND updated:0 WHILE some earlier run was active (a brand-new all-zero source never trips — a quiet corpus reads the same, maintenance §2's 0,0,0→frozen); (3) withdrawal_creep SOFT >5% / LOUD >15% — cumulative (withdrawn OR retired_upstream)/total documents, catching slow bleed the per-sync 20% breaker misses; (4) stale SOFT — enabled + live-policy source only, last_sync_at older than STALE_AFTER_DAYS=14 (manual/frozen expected to sit still); (5) never_synced INFO; sync_withdrawal reuses the creep thresholds for one sweep. SKIP RULE (the packet's think-it-through): a query is LOST (loud) only when its expected passage urn IS present in the catalog but Search fails to return it (the real loader/normalizer/indexer regression); when the urn is absent from the catalog entirely the source was simply never synced into THIS corpus → SKIPPED (informational). Per-urn presence (Store::Passage.first(urn:)) is more precise than a urn-scheme→slug map and needs no coupling to which sources a deployment happens to carry; documented in the class header. Corpus states: no catalog file → :absent ("no corpus — run sync/rebuild", replay skipped, exit 0); catalog but no fulltext table → :no_index (same informational stance). 2026-07-04 · P6-1 · 3a59aa3 · Structural-retry citation recovery in EpidocParser (the Iliad quarantine class). ROOT CAUSE: the CapiTainS subtype convention (div is a citation level iff @subtype == a cRefPattern unit name) fails whenever the header's unit labels don't match the body's subtype labels — the Iliad declares units book/line but labels its book divs subtype="Book" (case shift). FIX at the CTS-contract level: when (and ONLY when) the subtype pass raises a citation-shape ParseError (depth mismatch / missing @n / no citable passages / duplicate urn), the file is re-read matching the body against the deepest cRefPattern's replacementPattern XPATH with strict axis semantics ($-bound steps are citation levels, bare steps structural, child vs descendant axes honored, un-@n'd elements unselected) — i.e. exactly what the file's own declared resolver xpath selects; subtype labels stop mattering. Both passes failing → quarantine with a message naming both. FROZEN-URN ARGUMENT (P5-1 standard): retry runs strictly after the unchanged first pass raises, so cleanly-parsing docs never reach it — VERIFIED read-only vs live catalog: ALL 1,798 loaded perseus+first1k docs re-parsed → 0 urn mismatches, 0 text mismatches, 0 new errors; all 62 quarantined docs re-parsed → 58 recover (perseus 24/25 incl. the Iliad at 15,687 book.line passages; first1k 34/37). CENSUS (shape → count → outcome): depth-mismatch-fewer-than-declared P7+F12 → all recovered (case-shifted/renamed/unnamed subtype labels); depth-mismatch-more-than-declared F5 → recovered (extra same-label nesting is content under the strict xpath); no-citable-passages P12+F9 → 20 recovered (case-shifted units e.g. Exordium/Section, unit-less cRefPatterns e.g. Diodorus grc6), 1 STAYS (tlg1389 Harpocration: matchPattern declares 1 group but the xpath binds $1+$2 — self-contradictory header, honest quarantine "replacementPattern binds 2 component(s) but matchPattern declares 1"); missing-@n P6+F7 → recovered (un-@n'd elements are unaddressable by the declared xpath → structural noise, remaining units cite; Pindar tlg0033×4 mint fully); no-edition-div F3 → STAY (tlg0643.grc2/tlg3129/tlg4034 are div[@type="commentary"] files, nothing citable by the edition contract); duplicate-urn F1 → recovered (tlg0627: declared 1-level xpath selects the book divs — coarse but exactly what the declaration resolves to). WHY THE UNION CANNOT MISS: doc in language L is indexed as extra_L(generic(text)); the union always contains extra_L(generic(query)), so source-spelled queries always fold to the indexed form; and variants are ORed so the generic variant keeps no-rule languages findable (Gothic "jah" regression-tested against the lat j→i variant). REBUILD NOT PARSE-ONLY: content_sha256 covers text_normalized, so every passage hash changes BY DESIGN — a parse-only sync would journal a corpus-wide revision storm; the orchestrator runs full `nabu rebuild` (drop + re-derive from canonical, LOCAL) then replays goldens. Reads the live corpus only, writes exclusively under tmp, so the orchestrator runs it against the LIVE corpus at acceptance. 2026-07-07 · P7-6 · 1a85b93 · Show ranges: `nabu show URN:<start>-<end>` prints an INCLUSIVE, sequence-ordered slice of ONE document between two resolved citation suffixes — the concept's own syntax. THE PARSE PRECEDENCE (deliberate, documented, tested): (1) LITERAL FIRST — Show/Parallel resolve the whole string as a real passage or document urn before Range is ever consulted, so a passage urn that itself holds a hyphen stays reachable and is never misparsed as a range; (2) then split on the LAST hyphen (citation suffixes are dots+colons, never hyphens — 1.1, b2:5, r:3 — whereas the version segment perseus-grc2 / slug gothic-proiel carries a hyphen to the LEFT of the citation, so last-hyphen is unambiguous for every real corpus shape); the head is the absolute start passage urn, the tail is the END SUFFIX reconstructed against the SAME document (`<doc>:<end-suffix>`). (3) A range is RECOGNISED only when the head names a real passage OR a real document is a prefix of the head (so a bad START can be named "range start not found"); otherwise → nil → "urn not found", so a genuinely unknown urn is never dressed up as a range. SLICE = every passage whose STORED sequence lies in [start_seq, end_seq] inclusive, whatever citation shapes lie between — a papyri restart block (:b2, P5-1) is sliced straight through (`…:240:1-b2:2`). ERRORS (Query::Range::Error < Nabu::Error → CLI Thor::Error exit 1): endpoint-not-found names the failing endpoint's urn; start-after-end refused, suggesting a swap. New Nabu::Query::Range resolver (shared by Show + Parallel so they parse identically). Show.run gains `|| range(urn)` returning a RangeResult (document header shaped like DocumentResult so passage_label + --full-urn reuse unchanged, plus total M for the honest "[N of M passages]" note and the two endpoint urns). Parallel.locate gains a third return (in-slice suffix set); run filters aligned rows to the slice — pairing applies to the sliced rows only, unmatched suffixes stay one-sided (P7-4). CLI: print_show_range (header + range span + [N of M] + :suffix lines), rescue Range::Error in `show`, help show teaches range syntax with a CTS 1.1-1.10 example AND a papyri :1-b2:2 cross-block example. Tests: slice/inclusive/single/cross-block/endpoint-errors/reversed/literal-first (show_test), range+--parallel composition (parallel_test), CLI range render/full-urn/errors/help pins (cli_test). 2026-07-07 · P8-3 · af80d96 · Concordance: `nabu concord QUERY|--lemma FORM [--lang/--license/--limit/--width]` + MCP nabu_concord. KWIC formatter over Query::Search/LemmaSearch (Nabu::Query::Concord — a formatter, NOT a new query path): one row per hit, keyword column-aligned, left/right context trimmed to --width chars/side (default 40, … marks clip). DECISIONS: (a) fold-mapping — new Normalize.fold_with_map(text, language:) returns [folded, char-index map]; the keyword is located in the FOLDED passage form (same per-language P6-4 fold as the index) then mapped BACK to the PRISTINE accented text by index (the folds aren't length-preserving, so the map — not a naive index — is what makes ῆ line up under η). Pins byte-equality fold_with_map==search_form (Greek w/ combining marks) so the query, folded via search_form, is always found; prefix* keyword completes to the whole word (stops at space OR punctuation). Chose pristine display over showing the folded line — a concordance is for reading real usage. (b) occurrence policy — FIRST occurrence per passage, one row per hit (row count == hit count keeps the limit + MCP bounds contract clean; classic one-row-per-occurrence noted). (c) width default 40/side. (d) order — corpus (urn) order, re-sorted from the underlying query's page (Search by rank, LemmaSearch by urn), not rank order — a concordance is for scanning. Alignment: left context rendered to EXACTLY --width display chars (String#length; no East-Asian width), so the keyword's left edge is a fixed column; urn+[lang] tag per row. MCP nabu_concord is the 4th tool (tools/list count assertions updated across server/entrypoint/tools tests): same bounded (default 10/max 50, width max 120) + restricted-exclusion + license-fields-per-row + degradation contract as nabu_search, rows as structured left/keyword/right. 2026-07-08 · P9-4c · 7627a14 · GRETIL quarantine recovery (118 → 8). Census-first (orchestrator's 2026-07-08 census: 663 clean / 118 quarantined of 781 = 45 collision + 73 no-citable); three fixes, all frozen-urn-safe by construction, VERIFIED by a read-only two-parse census over every canonical file (663 clean docs byte-identical, 0 violations) AND the live parse-only sync (+110 added, ~0 updated, =663 SKIPPED, !8 errored — the loader's content_sha256 matched every previously-loaded doc, the standing frozen-urn proof). FIX 1 — the xml:id rung (~60 no-citable files: Rāmāyaṇa, Buddhacarita, Gītagovinda, Kirātārjunīya, Paippalāda Saṃhitā): `<lg xml:id="RgV_1.1.1">` with markerless `<l>` children → citation = the id, `RgV_` prefix stripped, dotted path kept (`1.1.1`); the lg IS the passage (its `<l>` are pada rows). CRITICAL DESIGN (the census caught it): rung d is NOT emitted in-line — it is a SECOND streaming pass (XmlIdExtraction) run ONLY when the primary rungs leave the doc empty. An in-line emit rewrote 144 already-loaded docs that carry `<lg xml:id>`/`<p xml:id>` AND prose and were loaded via the prose rung (their group text mashed into `pN` ordinals) — a frozen-urn violation. p-level xml:id is DELIBERATELY NOT recovered: a `<p xml:id>` carrying text already emits as a prose ordinal in the primary pass (clean-as-prose, frozen); recovering it would break the guard — flagged for a future packet. FIX 2 — single-pipe markers `| BBs_1,1.1 |` (~13 files, sa_bAdarAyaNa-brahmasUtra): the recognizer accepts `|`-delimited markers (matched-delimiter regex, `_<digit>` requirement rules out lone daṇḍas) but ALSO only as a fallback pass — keeping the primary MARKER byte-identical to P9-4b (`//`-only). Applying pipe in the primary pass broke 45 clean docs that merely contain `| … |` reading-text spans (read as prose before). FIX 3 — collision tolerance (45 files): a duplicate citation no longer quarantines; instead deterministic `:b2`/`:b3` suffixing in document order (ddbdp precedent — the real upstream dup Valc_1.70×2), PLUS a multi-prefix join for interleaved kārikā/commentary — when marker verses carry ≥2 distinct prefixes AND their bare numbers collide, the prefix joins the citation (DhvK_1.1/DhvA_1.1 → `DhvK.1.1`/`DhvA.1.1`). Both run in the primary pass but are provable no-ops on clean docs: collision-suffix fires only on duplicates (a clean doc has none, else it'd have quarantined), and multi-prefix is GATED on a real bare-number collision (the census found 26 files with ≥2 `//`-prefixes but only a handful collide — the rest were loaded cleanly with bare citations; unconditional prefixing would rewrite them). Single-prefix files never reach the join (guard test pins this). PERF: fallback order is xml:id BEFORE pipe — a markerless xml:id doc accumulates its whole body into one buffer, and running the `(//|\|)` recognizer over that megabyte buffer re-scans at every daṇḍa (quadratic, minutes on a purān_a); draining xml:id docs first keeps the pipe pass linear (pipe docs flush at every marker). RESIDUE — 8 no-citable stay quarantined, censused and REPORTED not force-fixed (packet scope): 4 genuinely unaddressable (paramArthasAra, bIjanighaNTu, lagadha-RgvedavedāṅgajyotiSa, vāmadeva — flat `<lg>`/`<l>`, zero `@n`/xml:id/marker/prose) + 4 recoverable marker-format variants OUT OF P9-4c SCOPE (vimalamitra-abhidharmadīpa `// Abhidh-d_N //` = hyphenated prefix the regex rejects; sātvatatantra/somānanda/puruSottamadeva `// Abbr_N</l>` = leading-`//`-only markers with the `</l>` as terminator, no closing delimiter) — a clean follow-up packet. Fixtures (4, trimmed real slices from local canonical, README + manifest updated): sa_RgvidhAna-a1 (xml:id), sa_bAdarAyaNa-brahmasUtra (pipe, whole), sa_AnandabhaTTa-vallAlacarita-c1 (real dup 1.70 → 1.70:b2), sa_Anandavardhana-dhvanyAloka-comm-u1 (DhvK/DhvA multi-prefix). Tests: per-fix urns+text, two-parse stability (all 7 fixtures), single-prefix guard (Brahmabindu stays bare `1`…`22`, never `BrbUp.N`), conformance green. Suite 925 green, lint clean. 02-sources GRETIL row updated (four rungs + recovery classes).

2026-07-09 · P10-4 · e2c47b4 · Per-treebank license override plumbing (fix: the two P10-2 Slavic treebanks are CC BY-SA 4.0 but `show`/MCP reported them `nc` because `documents.license_override` — honored by the whole query layer since P1-3 — had no write path; no adapter had ever set it). SEAM: the override rides `Nabu::Document#license_override` (nil default, the value object the loader already consumes on every persist path — both `load` and `load_from`, create AND update — so no new plumbing seam is invented; the alternative, DocumentRef, only reaches `load_from` and would need re-plumbing for the `load([doc])` path the loader tests use). Validated at construction via new `Model::Validation.license_class_or_nil!` (fail-fast at the domain boundary; the db CHECK on documents.license_override stays the backstop, not the UX). Adapter→Document flow: `UniversalDependencies::TREEBANKS` gains optional `:license`/`:license_class` (the two `old-east-slavic-*` entries set `attribution` / "CC BY-SA 4.0"; the four legacy entries omit them → override NULL → inherit the source's nc); `document_refs` carries `license_class` in the discover→parse `DocumentRef.metadata` hint channel ONLY when declared (legacy refs stay byte-identical); `ConlluParser#parse` gains a nil-default `license_override:` kw forwarded to Document (parser stays license-agnostic). REVISION SEMANTICS (the crux): `license_override` is deliberately kept OUT of `Store::ContentHash.document`, so a relabel cannot change content_sha256; the loader writes it on insert (`insert_document`) and on content-revise (`revise_document`), and — for the same-content case (override newly declared, changed, or removed upstream) — reconciles it on the SKIPPED path via new `reconcile_license_override?`, a pure metadata update modeled on `reconcile_retirement?`: no revision bump, no passage work, content_sha256 untouched, not journaled (matches how a title ride-along isn't its own event). An override removed from the map reverts the column to NULL on next load. TESTS: loader — `test_load_persists_license_override_on_create`, `test_relabel_on_reload_is_metadata_only_no_revision_bump_no_content_change` (pins revision==1 + content_sha256 unchanged across a nil→attribution relabel), `test_reload_with_same_override_is_idempotent` (skipped, no drift), `test_override_removed_upstream_reverts_to_null_on_next_load`, `test_content_revision_carries_the_current_override`, `test_invalid_license_override_is_rejected_before_any_write`; UD — `test_treebanks_map_sets_attribution_only_on_the_two_slavic_entries`, `test_parse_surfaces_license_override_for_slavic_and_nil_for_legacy`, `test_fixture_load_writes_attribution_override_only_for_the_slavic_treebanks` (end-to-end: two Slavic → attribution, four legacy → NULL, source class still nc). HEADLINE STRUCTURAL FINDS: (1) the div xml:id values ARE the canonical Cameron/DOE record numbers (A4.1 Beowulf, A32.1/A32.2 Cædmon's Hymn Northumbrian/West-Saxon) — unique across all 349, scholar-cited, so urn:nabu:aspr:<Cameron> replaces the packet's <poem-slug> sketch (title-slugs REJECTED on hard evidence: A43.5 and A43.10 are both <head>"For Loss of Cattle"); (2) despite NO l/@n, the per-div <l> ordinal EQUALS the printed ASPR line number (Beowulf div = exactly 3,182 <l>, Judith = 349 — both canonical counts), so ordinal citations are canonical here, NOT GRETIL-style honest-synthetic. FETCH-PATH DECISION (argued Phase A): Nabu::FileFetch, a ZipFetch SIBLING not a mode — ZipFetch is irreducibly zip-shaped (unzip, tree-root, multi-file set-difference); FileFetch keeps the contract verbatim (If-Modified-Since replay from .file-fetch.json, 304 → untouched, wiped-tree unconditional refetch, sha256 body pin, guard BEFORE mutation, GitFetch-format attic manifest) with the one genuine doomed case (a stale differently-named previous download; a changed body is an update, never atticked — the git precedent) and reuses ZipFetch.default_http (vendored-cert Faraday) by reference. PARSER: AsprParser, 7th family, deliberately the smallest (one uniform file) — UsfxParser one-file-many-docs shape (#texts inventory for discover, #parse extracts one div, stops at its end), XML::Reader only, one passage per <l> (sequence 0-based, citation 1-based ordinal), <unclear>/<foreign rune>/<g> text kept inline (canonical means canonical), head/bibl never leak. Fixture-time finds, both regression-tested: a div-level <gap/> BETWEEN lines (Riddles 82) must not shift ordinals; Nokogiri Reader reports whitespace-only nodes as TYPE_SIGNIFICANT_WHITESPACE — dropping them fused sibling runes ("DNLH." → captured, "D N L H.", while concatenate-then-collapse keeps dom<g>ę</g>… joins tight). ADAPTER: one document per poem, minting frozen; health probe rides :http_zip with HttpProbeTarget gaining optional state_file (default .zip-fetch.json — ORACC untouched) and nil metadata_url short-circuiting the license row to honest unchecked with NO GET (ASPR's license lives in-file; drift-on-refetch is the license watch). 2026-07-11 · P13-6 · f9f2b46 · Morph facets — `search --lemma X --morph case=dat,number=pl` over the gold shelves, one façade over three tagsets. DESIGN NOTE FIRST (conventions §6.1), verdicts argued from the LIVE data. Tagset reality (measured): CoNLL-U stores UD `feats` (`Case=Dat|Number=Plur`), PROIEL/TOROT a 10-position positional `morphology` tag (`-p---mgpwi`), ORACC a NER-flavoured `pos` (N/PN/GN/V…) with NO inflection. VOCABULARY VERDICT — unified UD façade, not per-family passthrough: query keys are UD feature names (case/number/gender/person/tense/mood/voice/degree, values dat, pl/sg, masc, aor, opt, sub…); CoNLL-U `feats` parsed as-is (already UD, zero translation); PROIEL positional tag DECODED position-by-position into the same UD names via a fixed 10×~8 code map (Query::MorphFacets::PROIEL_FIELDS; positions 9–10 = Germanic strong/weak + inflecting flag left undecoded — no clean UD facet, absence over a wrong map); ORACC has no inflectional morphology so inflectional facets NEVER match it (honest absence, tested), and a unified `pos` facet deliberately deferred (its tagset is not UD upos — welding a third scheme in would be dishonest for one field). Per-token family detection (has `morphology` → PROIEL, has `feats` → UD, else {}), so no source-family lookup. Tiny query language: comma-joined key=value ANDed, tiny value-alias table (sg→sing, pl→plur, du→dual; everything else IS the lowercased UD value). INDEX VERDICT — NO new index/migration: morphology post-filtered in Ruby over the lemma-anchored candidate passages' annotations_json. MEASURED on the live 1.94M-row lemma index (not assumed): `λόγος` dat-pl 37 ms/46 hits, `sum` subjunctive 720 ms/4129 hits, PROIEL orv `и` dat-pl 471 ms/537 hits, worst case (article ὁ) 757 ms/2255 hits — realistic content-word queries tens of ms, even the most common lemma sub-second; a facet index would multiply rows + need a rebuild for no interactive gain, and the lemma table's per-(passage,lemma) aggregation is the wrong granularity for per-token morph anyway. Morph test (cheap string parse) runs BEFORE the per-language fold so a selective facet folds only survivors; surface_forms + decoded `morph` evidence restricted to the MATCHING tokens (λόγος-in-two-cases surfaces only its dative-plural λόγοις). OUT OF SCOPE (honest): bare morph search without --lemma (would scan every annotated passage); ORACC pos-only facets; UD-vs-PROIEL tense/aspect encoding divergence follows each treebank's own convention (grc-perseus aorist = Aspect=Perf|Tense=Past). New lib/nabu/query/morph_facets.rb (parse/features/match?/describe + the PROIEL decode + UD passthrough); LemmaSearch#run gained `morph:` → run_with_morph (candidate_passage_ids pulls the WHOLE lemma set — morph is more selective than license so no pre-filter slice — then annotated_catalog_rows + morph_hit); Result gained `morph` (nil for plain hits, back-compat). Surfaces: `search --morph` (requires --lemma, malformed → Thor::Error) + evidence in print_lemma_results ({…}); MCP nabu_search gained a `morph` arg (requires lemma → InvalidArguments, malformed → InvalidArguments) + payload `morph` + description/schema. Scope: search/nabu_search only (concord/CLI-wide deferred). Demo (live db, read-only): `search --lemma λόγος --morph case=dat,number=pl --lang grc` → urn:nabu:proiel:greek-nt:20342 λόγος → λόγοις {number=plur|gender=masc|case=dat} "…ἐπὶ τοῖς λόγοις τῆς χάριτος…"; `--lemma богъ --morph case=dat,number=pl --lang orv` → urn:nabu:proiel:lav:130218 богъ → бгм҃ь {number=plur|gender=masc|case=dat}; `--lemma awīlu --morph case=dat --lang akk` → no matches (ORACC honest absence, lemma itself resolves). 2026-07-12 · P14-3 · 5c847ea · Vocab profiling — `nabu vocab URN [--limit N]` (the dropped P13-7, improvements §1.7). New `Nabu::Query::Vocab`: profiles a document / citation range / single passage against the whole gold-lemma corpus — total gold-lemma TOKENS, distinct lemmas, top DISTINCTIVE vocabulary, and in-document HAPAX legomena. Scope resolution is literal-first like Show (document || passage || range, reusing Query::Range); the tally parses only the scope's own passages' annotations_json (the cheap '"lemma"' substring guard + per-passage-language fold via Normalize.search_form, exactly as the Indexer folds), so token counts are exact; corpus baseline is the pre-built passage_lemmas index (passage-frequency, one indexed `lemma_folded IN(…)` GROUP BY, batched at 500 for SQLite's bind limit) + one `COUNT(*)`. METRIC = log-odds-ratio with an informative Dirichlet prior (Monroe, Colaresi & Quinn 2008), NOT the simple ratio the packet led with: measured on the live db, simple ratio floats near-hapax noise (alarius/liceor, doc-2/corpus-1, z-less) ABOVE the campaign vocabulary — the classic small-count blow-up — while the z-score's variance penalty ranks the real subject lexicon without any arbitrary min-count floor (Caesar → Caesar/hostis/castra/legio/proelium/exercitus; Cicero De officiis → officium/honestas/decorum/cupiditas/societas — validated). COVERAGE HONESTY: a document with zero gold tokens is not an error — it says so and names the gold-bearing languages straight from the lemma index (the only path that scans it, ~0.6s, once; normal path never does). COST (P13-6 measure-before-index precedent upheld): plain SELECTs, no new index — warm live timings Caesar 100ms, whole Vulgate NT (11,851 passages) 329ms, no-gold Beowulf 324ms, small ORACC Akkadian tablet 8ms; nothing exceeds ~350ms so a bespoke index would cost a rebuild to beat a sub-second post-filter. MCP verdict = CLI-only for v1, deferred (argued in the class note): unlike --random it IS research-facing, but an AI client gains little over nabu_search --lemma + nabu_define, and the 8% gold ceiling means it would answer "no gold lemmas" for most documents a model names (Homer/Vergil/papyri lack gold) — re-open when §3.1 lemma projection lifts coverage. Tests: test/query/vocab_test.rb (10, fixture treebank doc over a background corpus — totals, hapax, the log-odds-beats-singletons discrimination, --limit caps, range + single-passage scopes, no-gold honesty naming lat, withdrawn-excluded, unknown-urn NotFound). README command row added; docs/library.md §9 left for the gate. Suite 1590/26,584 green, lint 208 clean. Live db read-only throughout (delete-journal, SELECT-only, no mutation). One commit in worktree, not pushed.
2026-07-12 · P14-6 · 5c2135e · Incremental indexing — PHASE A MEASUREMENT ONLY (opus; no code, docs-only; STOP for owner decision). MEASURED cost ~70 s wall (2 runs): FTS5 insert ~36–37 s (~53%, the dominant phase), lemma build+insert ~23 s (~33%), catalog stream 6–10 s, alignment ~1.3 s (~2%), DDL negligible; NO ANALYZE/FTS5-optimize step exists (rebuild is clean-per-run — relevant to the incremental trade-off). Growth curve is EMPIRICAL not assumed (5-point FTS probe 1/2/3/3.76M): ~7–9 µs/row, gently rising = near-linear, mildly super-linear (segment-merge log factor); lemma tracks annotated-passage count (383k, 10.2%) NOT total N, alignment tracks registry NOT N. Projection: 5M ≈ 1.4–1.5 min, 10M ≈ 2.4–3 min (two scenarios on whether treebanks grow). Pain = two axes: absolute (crosses ~2 min ≈6–7M) and amplification (every per-source sync pays the whole corpus reindex — a ccmh sync = 340× over-index; per-source counts papyri 921k…freising 2k measured). Incremental options sketched with risk: (1) per-source reindex ~4–300× win, coarse/correct boundary — RECOMMENDED first; (2) dirty-doc tracking — finest but silent-staleness risk, forfeits the f(catalog) guarantee; (3) FTS5 tombstone deletes — needs periodic optimize the codebase lacks, worst simplicity/gain trade, skip. RECOMMENDATION: re-check-at-N, do NOT implement now (~70 s tolerable + provably correct; §4.2's "when it hurts" holds); trigger = interactive reindex crossing ~2 min (≈6–7M passages) or per-source cadence making the 340× amplification the daily annoyance. 2026-07-12 · P14-8 · 0ae8971 · Proximity search — `search A --near B [--window N]`, the TLG-style daily-use collocation probe, lemma-aware. Design-first + measure-first per the P13-6/P14-3 precedent, NO schema addition (as the packet expected): built entirely on FTS5 NEAR over the EXISTING boundary-folded index. NEAR semantics probed on SQLite 3.53, not assumed: `NEAR(a b, N)` = at most N tokens BETWEEN the phrases, order-independent, N=0 adjacent — exposed verbatim as `--window` (default 10, FTS5's own). The window counts FOLDED tokens (conventions §9): honest per-word for grc/lat/…, documented caveat for akk/sux where sign-joins/determinatives fold to spaces (one transliterated word = several tokens, window reads tighter). Fold-both-sides carried into NEAR: each side folds to the query_forms union, MATCH = OR of NEAR clauses over the cartesian product of the sides' variants (the P6-4 cannot-miss argument per side). Lemma-aware anchor: `--lemma X --near B` expands X → distinct attested folded surface forms via passage_lemmas (each folded by its passage language), each a NEAR phrase — εἶπε near κύριος counts as λέγω near κύριος; expansion is naturally bounded (folding collapses accent variants: ὁ→25, εἰμί→99, λέγω→140 forms; MAX_LEMMA_FORMS=400 guards FTS expression limits only); homograph imprecision documented honestly (no token offsets in FTS). New Query::Proximity shares Search's Result/snippet/bm25 + CatalogJoin, so hits render as plain search hits with BOTH terms bracketed. MCP nabu_search gains near + window (clamp 0–50). Out of scope, said in help/docs: cross-passage adjacency (passage = the unit; tested), --morph+--near (usage error), collocation statistics (Phase 15 menu — this returns the raw material), FTS operators inside proximity terms (phrase-quoted literal). Measured live (3.6M passages, read-only): κύριος NEAR θεός w5 grc 43–113 ms; λόγος NEAR θεός w5 24–37 ms — John 1:1 AND the P.Oxy. 8.1151 amulet quoting it, the intertext promise already visible; --lemma λέγω --near κύριος w3 = 280 NEAR clauses, 95–284 ms, surfacing the prophetic formula τάδε λέγει κύριος; pathological ὁ w3 79 ms. Tests: query/proximity_test (10 — grc + lat folds, lemma-expanded suppletive, window boundaries incl. N=0, order independence, filters, cross-passage honesty, anchor XOR), cli_test +5 (real UD fixture), mcp/tools_test +3. README row, mcp.md, search long_desc. Suite 1598/26,593 green, lint clean. One commit in the P14-8 worktree, not pushed.

2026-07-12 · P15-1 · a6e14d7 · parallels <urn> — passage-anchored intertext (the corpus reads itself; design doc docs/intertext-design.md §1, now architecture §13). Zero new schema, exactly as the design's live probes measured: Query::Parallels (lib/nabu/query/parallels.rb) folds the anchor to its stored search form, cuts overlapping 4-word grams, probes each as a quoted FTS5 phrase MATCH against the existing passages_fts, and scores candidates by shared-gram count WEIGHTED BY RARITY (1/document-frequency, df free from each probe's hit count) — a rare shared phrase (a real quotation) outweighs common function-word grams; grams in ≥500 passages dropped (no evidence + cost bound). 2026-07-12 · P15-2 · 1964db0 · Date/place axis, part 1 (design doc docs/intertext-design.md §3, now architecture §14). INTERNAL FABLE REVIEW of the date model BEFORE extractors (backlog P15-2): verdict "sound in structure — core arithmetic verified at every era boundary", with FIVE mandatory input-modelling fixes ALL incorporated. DATE MODEL (a reasoned deviation from the design doc's loose "astronomical years", argued openly): signed integer HISTORICAL years, negative = BCE, positive = CE, NO year 0 (1 BCE = -1, 1 CE = +1) — because HGV's OWN when="-0113" is labelled "113 v.Chr." (historical, not ISO-astronomical which would read 114 BCE) AND the CLI user's --from -300 means 300 BCE; ingest = source = query = display kills the whole BCE off-by-one class. Nabu::DateAxis owns it in one module (parse_year base-10 not Integer() [octal trap: "0700"→448], century_index/label/bounds, format_span), unit-tested across the reviewer's boundary table (101/100/1 BCE, 1/100/101 CE). REVIEWED FIXES: (1) reject year 0 loudly (Ruby floor-division would emit a phantom idx-0 "0th century"); (2) open-ended intervals — HGV notBefore-only/notAfter-only → one NULL bound = −∞/+∞, NULL-aware overlap so an open row never silently vanishes (335+ on disk); (3) multiple alternative origDates (dateAlternativeX/Y) → ENVELOPE (min lower, max upper); (4) .to_i not Integer() for zero-padded years; (5) label the by-not_before bucketing bias in vocab --by-century. Plus --century N shorthand (no hand-computed BCE bounds) and an F>T guard. SCHEMA: catalog-side document_axes (migration 008), NOT columns on documents — (document_id, not_before, not_after, precision, date_raw, place_name, place_ref, axis_source, passage_seq_from/to nullable for Part 2's chronicle grain). 2026-07-12 · P15-4 · 8d817c3 · Collation view — `align REF --collate [--base LABEL]` (design doc §2, now the P15-4 apparatus renderer over the alignment hub). Query::Collation (lib/nabu/query/collation.rb) is a pure RENDERER: it wraps Query::Align, runs it, transforms the aligned witness rows into an apparatus — zero schema, and the P11-8 range grammar + the P15-8 --long rule compose for free. GROUPING VERDICT, argued from the LIVE MARK 2.3 layout (not assumed): the collatable cell is the PAIR (language, script), NOT script alone (got/lat/eng/chu-CCMH are four languages in one Latin script — all present at MARK 2.3) and NOT language alone (chu holds both the Cyrillic PROIEL Marianus and the Helsinki-ASCII CCMH codices — the conventions-§9 fold cannot bridge them; downcasing Helsinki destroys S=š/E=ę). Script is detected from the TEXT (majority Unicode script, \p{Greek}/\p{Cyrillic}/\p{Latin}/…), because the language code does not record which transcription a witness uses — and this correctly caught that PROIEL "armenian-nt" is romanized (renders xcl/Latin, an aside). BASE VERDICT: the first witness of a cell in REGISTRY ORDER (the registry IS the display order — Align's own doctrine), --base LABEL|urn overrides per cell (validated across all witnesses, a miss is a caller error). DIFF: word-level LCS over RAW tokens (only punctuation-ONLY tokens dropped — a bare "."; every marker &/$/^/⸂⸃ kept verbatim, since stripping them destroys information exactly as folding does), a maximal run of deletes+inserts coalescing to one :sub — no transpose op, so a word-order variant is honestly del+ins (the Vulgate "ad eum ferentes" transposition, tested). Apparatus marks: `base → variant` (sub), `om. base` (omission), `add. variant` (insertion); agreements ELIDED (critic's apparatus style); cross-script/sole witnesses rendered UNDIFFED with the reason stated (:cross_script — a same-language witness exists in another script the fold can't bridge; :sole — the only witness of its language here); no_match/not_synced/withheld named once. --collate --long prints each witness's full tokens instead of the marks (one flag, both the range-cap-lift and the token expansion). GOLDEN reproduced through the production code against the live db at MARK 2.3: the four CCMH codices collate against base CCMH Assemanianus (придѫ/pridO→pridoSE, к&/k$→k&, ослабленъ/nosEqe→nosESte surfacing as real substitutions), the Cyrillic PROIEL Marianus set aside "different transcription system — not collated"; grc/Greek (PROIEL×SBLGNT, editorial brackets ⸂⸃ kept raw) and lat/Latin (PROIEL×Vulgate, the transposition) collate as clean secondary cells. MCP: nabu_align gains collate:true + base: (witness diff as type:"collation" — cells/asides/missing; the license gate WITHHOLDS excluded witnesses from the diff bodily, never leaking through an edits line, unless include_restricted). Tests: query/collation_test +15 (LCS insert/subst/omit/agreement isolated, (language,script) grouping, same-script-different-language separation, cross_script vs sole honesty, --base + miss-raises, --long full tokens, range per-ref apparatus, license withhold), cli_test +6 (apparatus + cross-script render, --base, --long-no-arrows, --base-without-collate error, base-miss error, help), mcp/tools_test +2 (collation payload contract + cross-script aside, restricted withheld + include_restricted). 2026-07-12 · P15-5 · 10b440d · Formula miner — `nabu formulas <source-slug|urn-prefix>` (design doc docs/intertext-design.md §5): intra-corpus repeated-n-gram mining, the oral-formulaic scholar's mirror of P15-1's parallels pointed INWARD (probe→count). Zero schema. Query::Formulas (lib/nabu/query/formulas.rb) reads text_normalized STRAIGHT from the catalog (no fulltext index, no Indexer touch — ctor takes only `catalog:`), streams the slice once (`dataset.each`), counts every gram in a Hash, keeps those recurring ≥min_count, ranks by count × gram-length, tops at --limit. SHARED MACHINERY, as the design named it: the "fold, elision strip, tokenize, shingle" was EXTRACTED to a mixin (lib/nabu/query/grams.rb — ELISION + gram_tokens + shingle(tokens,size)); Parallels and Formulas both `include Grams`, so a formula mined here re-probes as a parallel there, no drift. Parallels lost its private ELISION/gram_tokens/shingle to the module (GRAM_SIZE stays a Parallels constant — mcp/tools + cli reference it; shingle call now `shingle(tokens, GRAM_SIZE)`), behaviour byte-identical, its 12 tests green. SCOPE: a source slug (exact) else a DOCUMENT-urn byte-range prefix (urn >= p AND urn < p+maxcp — no LIKE to escape, rides the documents.urn unique index then joins passages by document_id); a document urn is a prefix of its passages' urns, so a whole work or the `urn:cts:greekLit:tlg0012` super-prefix (Iliad+Odyssey) scopes cleanly. An earlier passages.urn-OR variant defeated the index (Homer core 2.0 s → 0.23 s once dropped to documents.urn only); document-grain by design. LANGUAGE mandatory in practice (design §5): perseus-greek rides grc + eng on one slug, so `--lang` is offered and wanted when a source mixes translations (ASPR is single-lang, needs none); slice AND lang both apply through the shared CatalogJoin, exactly as Search. STOPWORD/RANKING VERDICT (the packet's ask): NO stoplist, NO df filter — rank by count × length and the ranking is SELF-FILTERING. Measured on live Homer grc: under a generous data-derived stopword definition (token in ≥10% of the slice's passages — δ 22%, καί 18%, δέ 15%) NOT ONE all-stopword 4-gram reaches the top 40; function words combine too freely to out-recur a genuine oral formula, and length rewards the contentful span. Rejected alternatives argued on the merits: (a) a per-language stoplist is a new unbounded per-language artifact (grc/lat/ang/orv/chu/got/san/akk/…, the "no clever registries" rule) that buys nothing the ranking doesn't; (b) a data-derived token-df filter MISFIRES on small slices — a formula's own content tokens have elevated df BY CONSTRUCTION, so it would eat the very formulas mined for. --min-count is the noise lever; the eye is the final filter, with almost nothing to reject. (At a fixed gram size count×length reduces to count; ×length is the general form and the discriminator once mixed sizes are mined — the natural v2, matching the design's `--n 3..5`.) LOCI: the lean pass keeps ≤3 example urns/gram (bounded); --long (house rule) re-walks the slice a SECOND time for EVERY locus of the few reported grams — pays its own ~0.2 s, compact prints "e.g. …". MCP: nabu_formulas deliberately NOT a v1 tool (argued in the class doc) — the MCP surface is passage-lookup-flavored, the miner is batch-flavored (streams a slice, returns a ranked table); natural home is the §7 batch/links surface. LIVE (read-only, through the production CLI): `formulas urn:cts:greekLit:tlg0012 --lang grc` → 27,903 passages / 199,816 tokens, 2,751 4-grams recur ≥3× (11.1% of gram instances), core 0.23 s — ὣς ἔφαθ' οἵ δ' 72×, τὸν δ' αὖτε προσέειπε 68×, τὸν δ' ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφη 55×, the …ἀπαμειβόμενος προσέφη πολύμητις Ὀδυσσεύς chain 50× (the design's exact numbers). `formulas aspr` → 30,550 / 175,736, core 0.15 s — ic wæs ond mid 13×, ond þæt word acwæð 12×, saga hwæt ic hatte 12×, Beowulf maþelode bearn Ecgþeowes 6×; `--gram-size 3`: hwæt ic hatte 16×, awa to feore 20×, to widan feore 19× (all three design 3-gram figures). Tests: query/formulas_test.rb +14 (mining/ranking, min-count floor, gram-size, no-stoplist pin, slug/prefix/unknown scope, lang filter across a two-language source, compact-vs-long loci, locus=passage dedupe, withdrawn, bad gram-size raise, slice totals), cli_test +6 (refrain+loci render, --long every locus, gram-size×min-count, unknown scope, bad gram-size exit 1, help).
